- **LIKWID family — likwid-topology/perfctr/pin/powermeter/mpirun/setFrequencies/features/genTopoCfg (8 binary stems via single multi-stem file)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh` via `-iname` + the round-116 `#compdef`-line multi-stem grep). Flag inventory transcribed directly from upstream [manpages.debian.org/bookworm/likwid/likwid-topology.1](https://manpages.debian.org/bookworm/likwid/likwid-topology.1.en.html) + `likwid-perfctr.1` + `likwid-pin.1` + `likwid-powermeter.1` + `likwid-mpirun.1` + `likwid-setFrequencies.1` (6 source-verified members; `features` and `genTopoCfg` covered as stubs since their man pages were not source-verified this round). Single multi-stem file `_likwid-topology` is `#compdef likwid-topology likwid-perfctr likwid-pin likwid-powermeter likwid-mpirun likwid-setFrequencies likwid-features likwid-genTopoCfg`, dispatching on `$service` — covers RRZE-HPC's performance toolkit for x86/ARM/POWER multi-core systems (the LIKWID = "Like I Knew What I'm Doing" tooling that's a staple of academic HPC perf work). The family shares a common short-flag style across all members: `-c cpu-list` (CPU expression — e.g. `0,1,2` or `0-7` or `S0:0-7@S1:8-15`), `-V`/`--verbose` level (0..3), `-v`/`--version`, `-h`/`--help`. **`likwid-topology`** (CPU/cache/NUMA introspection, 8 flags): `-g` ASCII-art topology (no GPU), `-c/--caches` detailed cache hierarchy, `-C/--clock` measure processor clock, `-G/--gpus` Nvidia GPU info, `-o/--output FILE` with suffix-driven filter (`.csv`/`.xml`/`.json` automatic). **`likwid-perfctr`** (hardware counter measurement, 22 flags + trailing command): mode switches `-m/--marker` (marker-API mode), `-a` (list available perf groups + exit), `-e` (list available counters + events + exit), `-H` (group-help with `-g`), `-i/--info` (cpuid + Intel PMU detail), `--stats` (always print stats table); selection `-c cpu-expr` vs `-C cpu-expr` (latter pins threads), `-g/--group GROUP`, `-G/--gpus gpu-list` + `-W/--gpugroup`, `-E search-str` (filter events by substring); modes `-t freq` (timeline), `-S waittime` (end-to-end via sleep), `-T time` (group-switch interval); output `-o/--output FILE`, `-O` (CSV); plumbing `-s/--skip hex-mask`, `-f/--force` (force register writes); trailing `*:::command:_command_names -e` for the wrapped process. **`likwid-pin`** (NUMA pinning launcher, 11 flags + trailing command): selection `-c`/`-C cpu-expr`, `-p` (print thread domains), `-d delim` (CPU delimiter); NUMA policy mutex `-i` (interleave) ↔ `-m` (membind); cleanup `-S/--sweep` (clean ccNUMA domains pre-run); `-s/--skip hex-mask`, `-q/--quiet`; trailing `*:::command:_command_names -e`. **`likwid-powermeter`** (RAPL-based power + temp readout, 10 flags): `-c socket-list`, `-M 0|1` (MSR access mode — 0=direct, 1=accessDaemon), `-s duration` (units `us`/`ms`/`s`), `-p` (dynamic clocks + CPI per socket), `-i/--info` (TDP + Turbo steps per RAPL domain), temperature mutex `-t` (Celsius) ↔ `-f` (Fahrenheit). **`likwid-mpirun`** (MPI launcher with pinning + counters, 14 flags + trailing command): MPI plumbing `-n`/`-np`/`--n`/`--np N` (4-way alias), `-hostfile FILE`, `-nperdomain N`, `-pin EXPR`, `-mpi intelmpi|openmpi|slurm|mvapich2` (4-value enum), `-omp intel|gnu` (hybrid OMP runtime); marker mode `-m/--marker`; output `-O` (CSV); passthrough `--mpiopts opts`; `-d/--debug`, `-s/--skip hex-mask`, trailing `*:::command:_command_names -e`. **`likwid-setFrequencies`** (CPU governor + freq control, 14 flags): info `-p` (current freqs), `-l` (configurable freqs), `-m` (configurable governors); apply `-c cpu-list`, `-g governor` (6-value enum: `performance`/`powersave`/`ondemand`/`conservative`/`schedutil`/`userspace`), `-f/--freq`, `-x/--min`/`-y/--max` constraints, `-t/--turbo 0|1`; Intel-only Uncore `--umin`/`--umax`, `--reset` (defaults + performance governor), `--ureset` (reset Uncore to max). **`likwid-features`/`likwid-genTopoCfg`** stub coverage (common short-flag conventions; man pages not source-verified this round so only the universal `-h`/`-v`/`-V`/`-c`/`-o` are modeled). **Blacklist additions (8)**: all 8 likwid stems inserted between `ligolo-proxy` (13785) and `lilo` (13786) in upstream-canonical order: `likwid-features` (f=102) < `likwid-genTopoCfg` (g=103) < `likwid-mpirun` (m=109) < `likwid-perfctr` (p,e=112,101) < `likwid-pin` (p,i=112,105) < `likwid-powermeter` (p,o=112,111) < `likwid-setFrequencies` (s=115) < `likwid-topology` (t=116). Sort verified position-by-position: at index 2 `ligolo`'s 'g' (103) < `likwid`'s 'k' (107) < `lilo`'s 'l' (108); within the `likwid-*` block, suffix order resolves correctly per the index-7+ table above. LC_ALL=C sort verified.
- **bsdtar (libarchive's tar implementation — default tar on macOS + FreeBSD)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh` via `-iname` + the round-116 `#compdef`-line multi-stem grep). Single-file completion `_bsdtar` covers libarchive's tar implementation — the default `tar` on macOS and FreeBSD; reads/writes 12+ archive formats (ustar/pax/cpio/zip/iso9660/ar/7zip/xar/mtree/etc) plus all the compression variants (gzip/bzip2/xz/compress/lzma/lzop/lrzip/lz4/zstd). ~80 flags grouped: 5-flag **mode mutex** (`-c`/`-x`/`-t`/`-r`/`-u`); 10-flag **compression mutex** (the 9 `-z`/`-j`/`-J`/`-Z`/`--lzma`/`--lzop`/`--lrzip`/`--lz4`/`--zstd` + auto-detect `-a/--auto-compress` — all exclude each other via a single shared `(-z --gzip ...)` zsh exclusion list); archive io `-f/--file` (- for stdin/stdout), `-b/--block-size N`, `@archive` (chain another archive). Extraction: mutex `-k/--keep-old-files`/`--keep-newer-files`, `-m/--modification-time`, `-O/--to-stdout`, `-U/--unlink-first`, `-p/--preserve-permissions`, `--safe-writes` (atomic temp-file extract), `-S` (sparse extraction). Path/link: `-P/--absolute-paths`, `-L/--dereference`, `-H`, `-h`, `-l/--check-links`, `--one-file-system`. Selection: `-C/--cd DIR`, `-T/--files-from FILE`, `-X/--exclude-from FILE`, repeatable `*--exclude PATTERN` + `*--include PATTERN`, `--exclude-vcs`, `-n/--no-recursion`, `--strip-components N`. Ownership: mutex `--same-owner`/`--no-same-owner`, `-o` (overloaded: ustar format in c/r/u, running uid in x), `--uid`/`--gid`/`--uname`/`--gname` overrides, `--numeric-owner`. **`--format` enum** (12 values: `ustar`/`pax`/`v7`/`cpio`/`shar`/`ar`/`mtree`/`iso9660`/`zip`/`7zip`/`xar`/`raw`), `--posix` (= `--format=pax`). Metadata mutex pairs: `--acls` ↔ `--no-acls`, `--xattrs` ↔ `--no-xattrs`, `--fflags` ↔ `--no-fflags` (BSD chflags). Date filtering: 8-flag time-cmp matrix `--newer`/`--newer-mtime`/`--newer-than`/`--newer-mtime-than` and the 4 `--older*` mirrors. Diagnostics: `-v/--verbose`, `-w/--confirmation/--interactive`, `-q/--fast-read`, `--totals`. Misc: `-s+ pattern` (regex name transform), repeatable `*--options opts` (module-specific behavior), `--use-compress-program PROG` (`_command_names -e`), `--null` (NUL-separated file list), `--passphrase PW`, `-B/--read-full-blocks` (GNU compat no-op). Repeatable trailing positional `*:file:_files` for the file/member list. `bsdtar` already in blacklist line 2550; no add needed.
- **Pelletier go-toml v2 family — tomljson + jsontoml + tomll (3 binary stems via single multi-stem file)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh` via `-iname` + the round-116 `#compdef`-line multi-stem grep). Single multi-stem file `_tomljson` is `#compdef tomljson jsontoml tomll`, dispatching on `$service` — covers Thomas Pelletier's pair of TOML↔JSON converters plus the in-place TOML linter/formatter from the same module. All three share the upstream `internal/cli/cli.go` argv-handling pattern (bare `flag.Parse()` + positional file or stdin), so the only meaningful CLI flag in the entire family is `jsontoml`'s `-use-json-number`. **`tomljson`** (TOML → JSON): `--help`, repeatable `*:TOML file (stdin if omitted):_files -g "*.(toml|tml)"` (covers both the canonical `.toml` and the historic `.tml` extension occasionally seen in older test corpora). **`jsontoml`** (JSON → TOML): `--help`, `-use-json-number` (preserves int/float precision by unmarshaling numbers as `json.Number` instead of `float64` — relevant for TOML round-trips of integer constants that would otherwise lose precision), repeatable `*:JSON file (stdin if omitted):_files -g "*.json"`. **`tomll`** (TOML lint/reformat): `--help`, repeatable `*:TOML file (lint + reformat in-place):_files -g "*.(toml|tml)"` — operates **in-place** by default per upstream `Inplace: true` in `cmd/tomll/main.go`, so positional completion intentionally doesn't gate on `-i`/`--in-place` flags (they don't exist). - **lziprecover (Antonio Diaz Diaz's data-recovery tool for the lzip format)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh` via `-iname` + the round-116 `#compdef`-line multi-stem grep). Flags transcribed directly from upstream [manpages.debian.org/bookworm/lziprecover/lziprecover.1](https://manpages.debian.org/bookworm/lziprecover/lziprecover.1.en.html). **Candidate-hunt dup-skip log this round (6 already-covered)**: `lzip`/`plzip` already at `more_src/_lzip` + `more_src/_plzip` (and `lzip-decompressor` covered as multi-stem via `src/_lzip-decompressor` `#compdef` line — caught by the round-116 grep upgrade), `pax` caught at stock zsh, `gron`/`huniq`/`fselect`/`sponge` (via multi-stem `more_src/_moreutils`) all already covered. `clzip`/`pdlzip` (C-only / public-domain lzip variants) truly fresh but share `lzip`'s flag set verbatim — could be added as multi-stem to `_lzip` in a future cleanup round; not a separate write. Single-file completion `_lziprecover` covers the data-recovery tool for the lzip format — repairs single-byte errors, splits multi-member archives, dumps/strips/removes corrupt members, and reproduces zeroed sectors using a known-good reference copy. ~26 flags grouped with 2 mutex sets: meta `-h/--help`, `-V/--version`. Core ops (each with `(...)` mutex against `-q` exclusion via `-v` selection): `-a/--trailing-error` (exit non-zero on trailing data), `-A/--alone-to-lz` (lzma-alone format conversion), `-c/--stdout`, `-d/--decompress`, `-D/--range-decompress N-M` (byte-range stdout dump), `-l/--list` (sizes), `-s/--split` (multi-member explode), `-t/--test` (integrity), `-f/--force`, `-k/--keep`. Repair-specific operations: `-e/--reproduce` (zeroed-sector reproduction via reference copy) + 3-flag tuning sub-group `--lzip-level N\|a\|m[N]` (single level / all / match length) / `--lzip-name NAME` (lzip executable, completes via `_command_names -e`) / `--reference-file FILE` (known-good `.lz` via glob); `-R/--repair` (single small-byte error repair); `-m/--merge` (correct errors using multiple corrupted copies of the same file). Output routing: `-o/--output FILE`, `-i/--ignore-errors`. Member-list operations (each takes a `[list]:d:t` spec — list of member ranges, `d` for damaged, `t` for trailing-data): `--dump SPEC` (dump to stdout), `--remove SPEC` (in-place removal), `--strip SPEC` (copy minus listed members). Verbosity mutex `-q/--quiet` ↔ repeatable `*-v/--verbose` (per upstream: `--quiet` cancels out `--verbose` and `-v -v` gives more detail than a single `-v`). Tolerance: `--loose-trailing` (allow trailing data that looks like a corrupt header). Repeatable positional `*:lzip file:_files -g "*.(lz|tlz|lzma)"` covers the 3 lzip-family extensions (.lz canonical / .tlz tar-bundled / .lzma legacy). `lziprecover` added to `blacklist.txt` at line 15184 between `lzip.lzip` and `lzless` (sort verified position-by-position: at index 4 `lzip.lzip`'s '.' (46) < `lziprecover`'s 'r' (114), and at index 2 `lziprecover`'s 'i' (105) < `lzless`'s 'l' (108)). LC_ALL=C sort verified.
- **zoo (Rahul Dhesi's classic .zoo archiver — Lempel-Ziv based, mid-80s era)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh` via `-iname` + the round-116 `#compdef`-line multi-stem grep). Command + modifier inventory transcribed from [manpages.org/zoo](https://manpages.org/zoo). **Candidate-hunt dup-skip log this round** (5 already-covered + 1 deferred): `hcxdumptool` already at `src/_hcxdumptool`, `hcxpcapngtool`/`hcxhashtool` covered via multi-stem `more_src/_hcxtools` `#compdef` line, `airbase-ng`/`aireplay-ng` already at `src/`; `unarj` (ARJ extraction-only sibling) truly fresh but every man-page mirror returned 404 (`manpages.debian.org/bookworm/arj/unarj.1` dyn-redirect, `manpages.ubuntu.com/manpages/jammy/man1/unarj.1`, `manpages.org/unarj` no-results) — deferred per the round-106 source-404 precedent. Single-file completion `_zoo` covers the classic .zoo archive format (still used for legacy PD shareware archives) — dual-mode CLI: a 17-letter "expert" single-character command verb or a hyphenated 10-verb "novice" form (`-add`/`-extract`/etc) that mirrors the same operations. 17 expert commands enumerated via `_expert` describe: `a` (add — overwrites if newer), `u` (update — newer-only), `c` (comment), `f` (filter — compress/decompress with M/u/h modifiers), `D` (delete inside archive), `e` (extract basename only), `g` (generate sub-archive — `A`/`q`/`+`/`-`/`=` modifiers), `h`/`H` (short/verbose help), `l`/`L` (short/long list), `P` (pack/squeeze), `T` (fix timestamp), `U` (undelete), `v`/`V` (verbose/full-verbose list), `x` (extract preserving paths). 10 novice commands enumerated via `_novice` describe: `-add`/`-freshen`/`-delete`/`-update`/`-extract`/`-move`/`-print`/`-list`/`-test`/`-comment`. Positional 1 uses `_alternative` to multiplex the two command surfaces — users get both expert and novice candidates in a single tab, with type tags distinguishing them. Positional 2 is the archive file (`_files -g "*.(zoo|ZOO)"` for case-insensitive matching since old DOS-era zoo files often used `.ZOO`). Trailing `*:file inside archive:_files` for the file-list arguments. The ~50 sub-command modifiers (e.g. extract modifiers `N`/`O`/`S`/`o`/`p`/`/`/`d`; list modifiers `a`/`A`/`c`/`C`/`d`/`f`/`g`/`m`/`q`/`v`/`V`/`@`/`/`/`1`/`+`/`-`; etc) are documented in the man page but not modeled here — zoo's modifier syntax concatenates them onto the command letter (e.g. `zoo vC archive` for list with column-aligned output) which doesn't tab-complete cleanly; left for manual entry. `zoo` added to `blacklist.txt` at line 29519 between `zoneminder` and `zookeeper-server` (sort verified position-by-position: at index 2 `zoneminder`'s 'n' (110) < `zoo`'s 'o' (111); within the `zoo*` block, `zoo` (length 3) < `zookeeper-server` (length 16) by shorter-string-wins on shared `zoo` prefix). LC_ALL=C sort verified.

Single-file completion `_arj` covers the open-source ARJ archiver — command-letter dispatch (`a`/`x`/`e`/`l`/`t`/etc) with a notorious 100+ switch tail organized in `-h*`/`-j*`/`-2*` prefix blocks. 27 commands enumerated via `_commands` describe: classic archive ops (`a`/`x`/`e`/`l`/`v`/`t`/`p`/`s`), modification (`d`/`f`/`u`/`m`/`n`/`o`/`r`/`g`/`c`/`y`), integrity/recovery (`i`/`q`/`w`), batch (`b`), housekeeping (`k`), join (`j`), plus 3 chapter-mode commands (`ac`/`cc`/`dc`) for chapter-archive workflow. ~25 most-used switches seeded (the upstream 100+ obscure `-hf4`/`-j#3`/`-2x1` long-tail left for power-users to type manually): meta `-help`; basic switches `-c` (skip time-stamp check), repeatable `*-e` (exclude paths), `-f` (freshen existing), repeatable `*-g PASSWORD` (garble password), `-i` (hide progress bar), `-m 0..4` (compression method enum), `-n` (only new files), `-r` (recurse), `-u` (update new + newer), `-v SIZE` (multi-volume), `-w DIR` (work directory), repeatable `*-x PATTERN` (exclude pattern), `-y` (assume yes); shifted `-h*` block — `-hk` (ARJ-PROTECT damage protection), `-hz` (ARJ-SECURITY envelope); shifted `-j*` block — `-jm` (max compression), `-jp` (paged), `-ji` (index file), `-je` (self-extracting), `-jf` (full paths), `-jt` (test temp archive), repeatable `*-jy` (suppress queries everywhere); shifted `-2*` block — `-2d` (DOS compat mode), `-2s` (preserve symlinks — UNIX), repeatable `*-2o` (store/restore ownership — UNIX). Positional 1 is the command letter (via `_commands` describe), positional 2 is the archive file (`_files -g "*.arj"`), and trailing `*: file:_files` for the file-list arguments. `arj` added to `blacklist.txt` at line 1292 between `arize-phoenix` and `arj-register` (sort verified position-by-position: at index 2 `arize-phoenix`'s 'i' (105) < `arj`'s 'j' (106); within the `arj*` block, `arj` (length 3) < `arj-register` (length 12) by shorter-string-wins on shared `arj` prefix). LC_ALL=C sort verified.
- **vnu (W3C Nu HTML/CSS/SVG validator — Java)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh` via `-iname`). Flags transcribed directly from upstream [validator.github.io/validator/docs/vnu.1.html](https://validator.github.io/validator/docs/vnu.1.html) OPTIONS section. **Candidate-hunt dup-skip log this round (substantial multi-stem catch)**: hit a beautifully misleading 6-stem false-positive — `aunpack`/`apack`/`als`/`acat`/`adiff`/`arepack` all flagged FRESH because `find -iname "_aunpack"` etc. returned nothing, but the existing `more_src/_atool` is multi-stem `#compdef atool aunpack apack als acat adiff arepack` so all 6 are already covered. **Reinforces the round-104 case-insensitivity finding**: a name-based `find` (even with `-iname`) misses multi-stem coverage entirely — must check the `#compdef` line of existing files to detect this class of dup. Also already-covered: `atool`/`dtrx`/`cmark`/`cmark-gfm`/`htmlhint`. Single-file completion `_vnu` covers the Nu HTML Checker (Java-based — invoked as `java -jar vnu.jar` or the `vnu` wrapper script) — validates URLs/files/directories against W3C schemas for HTML5+/CSS/SVG/XHTML. Sister binaries `vnu-server`/`vnu-client` expose the same checker over HTTP and are out of scope for this completion. ~27 flags grouped with 3 mutex sets: meta `--help`, `--version`. Message filtering: `--asciiquotes` (smart-quote substitution in messages); mutex `--skip-info-messages` ↔ `--errors-only`; `--Werror` (any warning → non-zero exit), `--exit-zero-always` (always 0 even with errors), `--stdout` (errors to stdout not stderr); `--filterfile FILE` (regex pattern file) + repeatable `*--filterpattern REGEX` for selective message suppression. Output format: `--format gnu\|xml\|json\|text` (full upstream enum). **Document-type dispatch mutex** (7-flag exclusion group — only one can be active at a time): `--skip-non-css`/`--css` for CSS-only mode, `--skip-non-svg`/`--svg` for SVG-only mode, `--skip-non-html`/`--html`/`--xml` for parser selection on HTML/XHTML files. Cross-type opt-ins (not in the mutex group since they're additive): `--also-check-css` and `--also-check-svg` for checking CSS+SVG alongside HTML. HTTP fetch: `--user-agent UA-STRING`, repeatable `*--additional-request-header "HEADER: VALUE"` for custom request headers when validating remote URLs. Parser behavior: `--no-langdetect` (skip language detection + `html[lang]` check), `--no-stream` (force buffered instead of streaming parse). Diagnostic: `--verbose` (print file names being checked). Synopsis-only flags reproduced with best-guess arg types: repeatable `*--entities` (extra entity defs) and `--schema URL-OR-FILE` (non-default schema override). Repeatable positional `*:URL/file/directory:_files` covers the three input forms vnu accepts. `vnu` added to `blacklist.txt` at line 27544 between `vnstati` and `void` (sort verified position-by-position: at index 1 both share 'n' (110), so resolves at index 2 — `vnstati`'s 's' (115) < `vnu`'s 'u' (117); and at index 1 `vnu`'s 'n' (110) < `void`'s 'o' (111)). LC_ALL=C sort verified.
- **when (Leon Brocard's tiny personal calendar utility)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh` via `-iname`). Flags + command codes transcribed from upstream [manpages.debian.org/bookworm/when/when.1](https://manpages.debian.org/bookworm/when/when.1.en.html). **Candidate-hunt dup-skip log this round (substantial — 12 caught + 2 deferred)**: 10 already-covered candidates `tdl`/`icdiff`/`pcre2grep`/`deheader`/`cppman`/`calcurse`/`remind`/`pueue`/`autorestic` plus the round-113-promised `strongswan` — `swanctl` man page sourced cleanly but the **stock zsh** at `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh/functions/_swanctl` already ships a `_swanctl` (and similarly `_ipsec`), so neither can be added; the `strongswan` umbrella binary's own man page returned 404 across `manpages.debian.org` dyn-redirect, `man.archlinux.org/man/strongswan.8.en`, and `wiki.strongswan.org/projects/strongswan/wiki/Strongswanctl` (Anubis access-denied) — deferred per the round-106/108/109/111/113 source-404 precedent. `ts` (task spooler) explored as fresh + in blacklist but skipped because the `ts` binary name collides with the unrelated `moreutils ts` timestamp filter — writing a single `_ts` would mismatch one of the two tools depending on which the user installed; deferred for proper multi-tool detection in a future round. Single-file completion `_when` covers the single-file calendar (default `~/.when/calendar`, one line per event) — long-form-only flags drive rendering and an 8-letter positional command code that can be **combined** (e.g. `when cw` = calendars then weekly items, `when iy` = items then year view). 8 command codes via `_verbs` describe: `i` (default — upcoming items), `c` (last/this/next month calendar grids without items), `e` (open `$EDITOR` on the calendar file), `w`/`m`/`y` (coming week/month/year items), `j` (modified Julian day for date arithmetic), `d` (current date only). ~36 long-form flags grouped with 9 mutex pairs encoded in zsh exclusion sets: meta `--help`/`--version`; window control `--language LANG`, `--future DAYS` (default 14), `--past DAYS` (default -1), `--calendar FILE`, `--editor COMMAND` (default `emacs -nw` — completes via `_command_names -e`); wrap mutex `--wrap COLS` / `--wrap_auto` ↔ `--noowrap_auto` / `--wrap_max COLS`; rows mutex `--rows ROWS` (default 40) / `--rows_auto` ↔ `--norows_auto`; header mutex `--header` ↔ `--noheader`; pager mutex `--paging` ↔ `--nopaging` + `--paging_less_options OPTS`; styling `--filter_accents_on_output`, `--styled_output`, `--styled_output_if_not_tty`, `--calendar_today_style STYLE`, `--items_today_style STYLE`; pre-processing `--prefilter PROGRAM` (`_command_names -e`); date control `--now "Y M D"` (override current date); month rendering mutex `--neighboring_months` ↔ `--noneighboring_months`; week-start mutex `--monday_first` ↔ `--nomonday_first`; Easter `--orthodox_easter`; time format mutex `--ampm` ↔ `--noampm` + `--auto_pm HOUR` (assume PM for hours below X); entry expansion mutex `--literal_only` ↔ `--noliteral_only`. `when` added to `blacklist.txt` at line 27913 between `wheel3.9` and `whence` (sort verified position-by-position: at index 3 `wheel3.9`'s 'e' (101) < `when`'s 'n' (110), and at index 4 `when` ends < `whence`'s 'c' (99) — wait, 'c' is 99 not nothing; correct comparison: `when` length-4 vs `whence` length-6, shared prefix `when`, so `when` < `whence` by shorter-string-wins). LC_ALL=C sort verified.

Single-file completion `_wg-quick` covers Jason Donenfeld's `wg(8)` setup wrapper — reads `/etc/wireguard/<INTERFACE>.conf` for Address/DNS/MTU/Table/PreUp/PostUp/PreDown/PostDown/SaveConfig directives, then drives `wg` + `ip(8)` accordingly. 4 verbs via `_verbs` describe: `up` (add and set up interface — Address/MTU/routes/PreUp/PostUp), `down` (tear down — PreDown/PostDown), `save` (save current state into config), `strip` (dump config with wg-quick-only directives stripped — pipe-friendly for `wg setconf`). 1 GNU-style flag: `-h/--help`. **Live-interface helper `_wg_quick_interfaces`** walks `/etc/wireguard/*.conf` with zsh nullglob `(N)`, strips the leading directory and trailing `.conf` via `:t:r` modifier (`/etc/wireguard/wg0.conf` → `wg0`), so the user-visible candidate is the bare interface name — matching how `wg-quick up wg0` is invoked in practice. Positional 2 uses `_alternative` to multiplex two surfaces: config-file path completion (`_files -g "*.conf"`) for absolute paths, plus the live-interface describe for the bare-name shortcut. `wg-quick` already in `blacklist.txt` at line 27890; no add needed.
- **djvumake (Yann Le Cun & Léon Bottou's DjVu chunk assembler)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh` via `-iname`). Chunk inventory transcribed from upstream [manpages.debian.org/bookworm/djvulibre-bin/djvumake.1](https://manpages.debian.org/bookworm/djvulibre-bin/djvumake.1.en.html). **Candidate-hunt dup-skip log this round** (5 already-covered + 4 fresh-but-no-completion-worthy-surface): `djvused`/`djview`/`djvuextract`/`djvups`/`bcal`/`dasel`/`sshs`/`hck` all caught as already covered. `djvumake` is the only fresh DjVu-family binary with a real CLI surface — the others (`djvm`/`djvmcvt`/`djvudigital`/`djvutoxml`) have known but already-covered completions in `man_src/`/`src/`. Single-file completion `_djvumake` covers the DjVu chunk assembler — builds a `.djvu` file from raw chunk fragments via a non-standard `CHUNKID=value` argument syntax (not GNU-style flags). 13 chunk types in the `_chunks` describe array (with key=value suffix-suppression for tab-completion): `INFO=` (initial info chunk W,H,DPI default 300), `Sjbz=` (JB2 foreground mask), `Smmr=` (MMR/G4 mask), `BG44=` (IW44 background — `file[:N]` for multiple chunks), `BGjp=` (JPEG background), `BG2k=` (JPEG-2000 background), `FGbz=` (foreground colour — file or `{#color[:x,y,w,h]}`), `FG44=`/`FGjp=`/`FG2k=` (foreground colour in IW44/JPEG/JP2 respectively), `INCL=` (DjVu3 include chunk for multipage), `Djbz=` (JB2 shape-dictionary), `PPM=` (emit IW44 BG + FG colour chunks from a PPM). 1 GNU-style flag: `-h`. Positional 1 is the output `.djvu` file (via `_files -g "*.djvu"`), repeatable positional 2+ accept chunk specs. The `_describe -S ''` suffix-suppression keeps zsh from auto-inserting a space after the `=` so the user can immediately continue typing the chunk argument. `djvumake` added to `blacklist.txt` at line 6318 between `djvuextract` and `djvups` (sort verified position-by-position: at index 4 `djvuextract`'s 'e' (101) < `djvumake`'s 'm' (109) < `djvups`'s 'p' (112)). LC_ALL=C sort verified.
- **pngnq (Stuart Coyle's NeuQuant-based PNG palette quantizer)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh` via `-iname`). Flags transcribed directly from [manpages.debian.org/bookworm/pngnq/pngnq.1](https://manpages.debian.org/bookworm/pngnq/pngnq.1.en.html). **Candidate-hunt dup-skip log this round** (4 caught + 1 deferred): `apngasm` (animated PNG assembler) explored as fresh but uses non-standard Windows-style slash flags (`/kp` keep-palette, `/kc` keep-color, `/f` invisible-frame) plus undocumented numeric frame-delay positionals — encoded as ad-hoc zsh _arguments couldn't model the slash syntax cleanly, deferred; `apngdis` (animated PNG disassembler) confirmed via man page to have **zero options** (just `filename.png [name-prefix]` positionals) — no completion-worthy surface, deferred; `gif2png` truly fresh but every man-page mirror returned cert/404 errors (`catb.org` TLS-cert-altname-invalid, `gitlab.com/esr/gif2png/raw/master/gif2png.c` 404, `manpages.ubuntu.com/manpages/jammy/man1/gif2png.1` 404) — deferred per round-106/108 source-404 precedent; `rsvg-convert`/`svgo`/`pup`/`hq` all caught as already covered. Single-file completion `_pngnq` covers the NeuQuant-based PNG palette reducer — maps full-color PNG → 8-bit palette PNG for smaller file size, optional Floyd-Steinberg dithering, default output suffix `-nq8.png`. 10 flags + repeatable positional: meta `-h`, `-V` (version + library versions — the uppercase `-V` distinguishes from the lowercase `-v` verbosity flag, an unusual convention worth honoring); diagnostic `-v` (verbose status messages); safety `-f` (force overwrite existing output); algorithm tuning `-s FACTOR` (NeuQuant sample factor — default 3, higher = faster + less accurate), `-n COLORS` (target palette size — 2..256, default 256), `-Q n\|f` (dither method enum — `n` = no dither/default, `f` = Floyd-Steinberg), `-g GAMMA` (image gamma override — defaults to reading the source PNG's gAMA chunk, falls back 1.0); output routing `-e SUFFIX` (filename suffix override, default `-nq8.png`), `-d DIR` (output directory override — useful for keeping originals untouched); repeatable positional `*:input PNG (stdin if omitted):_files -g "*.png"`. The `-Q n|f` dither enum is encoded as a 2-value choice list so users can't mistype it; sample-factor, color-count, and gamma are left as bare-numeric prompts (no enum) since the upstream-documented "good default" (3) is just a starting hint. `pngnq` added to `blacklist.txt` at line 19993 between `pngfix` and `pngquant` (sort verified position-by-position: at index 3 `pngfix`'s 'f' (102) < `pngnq`'s 'n' (110) < `pngquant`'s 'q' (113)). LC_ALL=C sort verified.

Single-file completion `_jpeginfo` covers the libjpeg-based info/integrity tool — dimensions, JPEG coding, optional MD5/SHA-256/SHA-512 checksums, and `-d`-delete-on-error workflow. 18 flags + repeatable positional: meta `-h/--help`, `--version`; integrity `-c/--check` (scan beyond headers), `-C/--comments` (dump COM markers), `-d/--delete` (delete files with errors), `-m/--mode all\|erronly` (delete-mode selector, only meaningful with `-d`); input source `-f/--file LIST-FILE` (read filenames from file, `-` = stdin), `--stdin` and bare `-` (read image data from stdin); checksums `-2/--sha256`, `--sha512`, `-5/--md5` (three independent hash flags — can stack); detail `-i/--info` (extended: coding/density/CCIR601), `-H/--header` (column header row), `-v/--verbose`; **output-format mutex group** (4 flags, only one valid at a time) `-l/--lsstyle` ↔ `-j/--json` ↔ `-s/--csv` ↔ `-q/--quiet` — encoded as a single `(... ... ... ...)` exclusion list so zsh suppresses the dominated format flags once the user picks one. Repeatable positional `*:jpeg file:_files -g "*.(jpg|jpeg|jpe|jfif|jif)"` covers the 5 historical JPEG file extensions (`.jpg`/`.jpeg` modern + `.jpe` short DOS + `.jfif`/`.jif` raw JFIF). `jpeginfo` added to `blacklist.txt` at line 12368 between `jpegexiforient` and `jpegoptim` (sort verified position-by-position: at index 4 `jpegexiforient`'s 'e' (101) < `jpeginfo`'s 'i' (105) < `jpegoptim`'s 'o' (111)). - **Joern family — joern + joern-cli + joern-parse + joern-export + joern-scan + joern-slice + joern-flow + joern-vectors + joern-stats (9 binary stems via single multi-stem file)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh` via `-iname`). Flags transcribed directly from upstream Scala scopt argument parsers under [joernio/joern](https://github.com/joernio/joern) `joern-cli/src/main/scala/io/joern/joerncli/` — `JoernParse.scala`, `JoernExport.scala`, `JoernScan.scala`, `JoernSlice.scala`, `JoernFlow.scala`, `JoernVectors.scala`. Single multi-stem file `_joern` is `#compdef joern joern-cli joern-parse joern-export joern-scan joern-slice joern-flow joern-vectors joern-stats`, dispatching on `$service` — covers Whitespace Engineering's static code-analysis platform built around CPGs (Code Property Graphs). **`joern`/`joern-cli`** (interactive Scala REPL launcher): `--help`, `--script FILE` (run script instead of REPL, `.sc`/`.scala` glob), `*--param key=value`, `--import-script FILE`, `--server`/`--server-host HOST`/`--server-port PORT` (JSON-RPC server mode), `--nocolors`. **`joern-parse`** (source → CPG): `-o/--output FILE`, `--language` with 14-frontend enum (`c`/`cpp`/`java`/`jvm`/`javasrc`/`go`/`python`/`php`/`csharp`/`kotlin`/`js`/`javascript`/`ruby`/`swift`/`ghidra`), `--list-languages`, `--namespaces NS,NS`, mutex `--nooverlays` ↔ `--overlaysonly`, `--max-num-def N` (data-flow definition limit), trailing frontend-args after `--`. **`joern-export`** (CPG → graph format): `-o/--out DIR`, `--repr` (7-value: ast/cfg/ddg/cdg/pdg/cpg14/cpg/all, default cpg14), `--format` (4-value: dot/neo4jcsv/graphml/graphson). **`joern-scan`** (run query scans): `--overwrite`, `--store`, `--dump`/`--dump-to FILE`, `--list-query-names`, `--updatedb`/`--dbversion`, `--names NAMES,NAMES` and `--tags TAGS,TAGS` query-set filters, `--depth N` interprocedural call depth, `--language`/`--list-languages` (12-frontend enum). **`joern-slice`** (CPG slicing — state-machine sub-tree with 2 modes): common flags `-o/--out`, `--dummy-types`, `--file-filter`/`--method-name-filter`/`--method-parameter-filter`/`--method-annotation-filter` regex filters, `-p/--parallelism N`; **`data-flow` mode** adds `--slice-depth N` (default 20), `--sink-filter REGEX`, `--end-at-external-method`; **`usages` mode** adds `--min-num-calls N` (default 1), `--exclude-operators`, `--exclude-source`. **`joern-flow`** (data-flow query): 3 positionals `src-regex`/`dst-regex`/`cpg-file`, plus `--src-param N`/`--dst-param N`/`--depth N`/`--verbose`. **`joern-vectors`** (CPG → vectors): `-o/--out DIR`, `--features` flag, positional CPG. **`joern-stats`** (minimal flag set — scopt config not exposed): `--help` + CPG positional. **Blacklist additions (9)**: `joern`, `joern-cli`, `joern-export`, `joern-flow`, `joern-parse`, `joern-scan`, `joern-slice`, `joern-stats`, `joern-vectors` inserted between `joe` and `john` — sort verified position-by-position: at index 2 `joe`'s 'e' (101) = `joern`'s 'e' (101), so `joe` < `joern` by shorter-string-wins (length 3 < 5); within the `joern-*` block, suffix order resolves as `cli` (c=99) < `export` (e=101) < `flow` (f=102) < `parse` (p=112) < `scan` (sc=115,99) < `slice` (sl=115,108) < `stats` (st=115,116) < `vectors` (v=118); finally at index 2 `joern`'s 'e' (101) < `john`'s 'h' (104). LC_ALL=C sort verified.

- **shellcraft (pwntools' shellcode generator with hierarchical shellcode catalog)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh` — used the upgraded `-iname` (case-insensitive) dup-check this round following last round's macOS HFS+/APFS case-insensitivity gotcha). Flags transcribed directly from upstream [docs.pwntools.com/en/stable/commandline.html](https://docs.pwntools.com/en/stable/commandline.html) options table plus the `pwn` global-flag table. Single-file completion `_shellcraft` covers Gallopsled's standalone `shellcraft` binary (also reachable as `pwn shellcraft <name>`); generates pre-built shellcodes from a hierarchical catalog (architecture `.` os `.` payload — e.g. `amd64.linux.sh`, `i386.linux.dupsh`, `arm.linux.execve`, `aarch64.linux.sh`, `mips.linux.sh`, `thumb.linux.sh`) with per-name argument lists, plus encoding/output transformations applied after generation. ~20 flags grouped: meta `-h/--help`, `-?/--show` (per-name doc), `-l/--list` (catalog browse, optional filter), `--syscalls` (list all syscalls for selected arch+os, exit); output `-o/--out FILE`, `-f/--format` with the full 18-value upstream enum table (`r`/`raw`, `s`/`str`/`string`, `c`, `h`/`hex`, `a`/`asm`/`assembly`, `p`, `i`/`hexii`, `e`/`elf`, `d`/`escaped`, `default`); debug `-d/--debug` (auto-launch GDB), `-b/--before` and `-a/--after` (insert debug-trap markers around emitted code), `--delim` (multi-shellcode separator); bad-byte encoding `-v/--avoid HEX-BYTES`, `-n/--newline`, `-z/--zero` (NULL-byte avoid — the three classic shellcode-encoding constraints); execution `-r/--run` (run the generated shellcode in-process for quick smoke-test), `--address HEX` (load-address override); ELF emission `-s/--shared` (build shared-library ELF instead of raw blob); pwn-global overrides `--arch` (11-value enum `i386`/`amd64`/`arm`/`aarch64`/`thumb`/`mips`/`mipsel`/`mips64`/`mips64el`/`powerpc`/`sparc`), `--os` (5-value enum `linux`/`freebsd`/`windows`/`baremetal`/`android`); color mutex `--color` ↔ `--no-color`. **`_names` catalog** seeds the positional argument with 21 of the most common CTF picks (amd64+i386+arm+aarch64+mips+thumb x sh/execve/dupsh/read/write/open/connect/listen/cat) plus common synthetic `common.{nop,infloop,debugbreak}` — users still tab through arbitrary names since the upstream catalog is much larger than this seed. Positional argument 2+ is the shellcode-specific argument list (e.g. `i386.linux.read 3 0x8048000 100` for read(fd, buf, len)) — left as free-form `*:shellcode argument:` since arg semantics depend entirely on which shellcode is selected. `shellcraft` added to `blacklist.txt` at line 23534 between `shellcheck` and `shellharden` (sort verified position-by-position: at index 5 both `shellcheck` and `shellcraft` share 'c' (99), so resolves at index 6 — `shellcheck`'s 'h' (104) < `shellcraft`'s 'r' (114); and `shellcraft`'s index-5 'c' (99) < `shellharden`'s index-5 'h' (104)). LC_ALL=C sort verified.
- **one_gadget (David Wang's libc "one gadget RCE" finder)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh`) — flags transcribed directly from upstream [github.com/david942j/one_gadget](https://github.com/david942j/one_gadget) README options table. Single-file completion `_one_gadget` covers the Ruby tool that locates the single-instruction `execve("/bin/sh", NULL, NULL)` shortcut inside a libc image — the bread-and-butter primitive for libc-leak exploits in pwn CTF. **Candidate-hunt dup-skip log**: round 104 fresh-check turned up `ROPgadget` (Jonathan Salwan's ROP gadget finder) which was correctly skipped — existing `more_src/_ROPgadget` (canonical filename `_ropgadget` on disk; macOS HFS+/APFS case-insensitive resolves both spellings) already declares `#compdef ROPgadget ropgadget` with comprehensive flag coverage including `--rawArch`/`--rawMode`/`--rawEndian` capstone enums and `--mipsrop` MIPS-specific dispatch. Note for future fresh-checks: case-insensitive macOS filesystems make `find -name` (case-sensitive) lie about what's already on disk — the file walker resolved the file as `_ropgadget` even though the dup-check name was `_ROPgadget`. 12 flags: meta `-h/--help`, `--version`, `--info BuildID` (show version info for a specific libc BuildID without lookup). Input source: `-b/--build-id BuildID` (SHA1 BuildID lookup against bundled db) versus libc-file positional via `_files -g "*libc*"` — repeatable; mutex `-f/--force-file` ↔ `--no-force-file` controls precedence between file-first vs BuildID-first lookup. Output: `-l/--level 0|1|2|3` (verbosity — higher reveals more conditional/marginal gadgets), `-o/--output-format pretty|raw|json` and `-r/--raw` shorthand (both wired into the same mutex group so zsh suppresses the dominated flag); `-n/--near FUNCTIONS-OR-FILE` orders results by proximity to specified ELF functions or GOT entries (completes via `_files`). Exploit-integration: `-s/--script EXPLOIT-SCRIPT` (execute script per-gadget with the offset as `$1` — heavily used in CTF auto-pwn pipelines); `--base HEX-ADDRESS` (libc base override, default 0). `one_gadget` added to `blacklist.txt` at line 18150 between `ondir` and `oneagent` (sort verified position-by-position: at index 2 `ondir`'s 'd' (100) < `one_gadget`/`oneagent` shared 'e' (101), then at index 3 `one_gadget`'s '_' (95) < `oneagent`'s 'a' (97) — underscore precedes lowercase letters in ASCII so `one_gadget` slots ahead of the `onea*` block). LC_ALL=C sort verified.
- **pwninit (Andrew Otto's CTF binary-exploit challenge initializer)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh`) — flags extracted directly from upstream [github.com/io12/pwninit](https://github.com/io12/pwninit) `src/opts.rs` (structopt definitions that generate clap args). Single-file completion `_pwninit` covers the auto-detection + patchelf + pwntools-template-emission flow used at the start of every pwn CTF challenge. 11 flags: meta `-h/--help`, `-V/--version`. Auto-detect overrides: `--bin FILE` (challenge binary), `--libc FILE` (challenge libc, completes via `_files -g "*libc*"`), `--ld FILE` (linker for libc preload, completes via `_files -g "*ld*"`). Template customization: `--template-path FILE` (custom pwntools solve-script template, completes via `_files -g "*.py"`), `--template-bin-name NAME` (binary-variable name in emitted template, default `exe`), `--template-libc-name NAME` (default `libc`), `--template-ld-name NAME` (default `ld`). Disable switches: `--no-patch-bin` (skip patchelf), `--no-template` (skip solve-script emission). All file-completion specs use targeted globs — `*libc*` matches the typical CTF naming convention (`libc.so.6`, `libc-2.31.so`, `libc6_2.27-3ubuntu1_amd64.deb`-extracted), `*ld*` matches `ld-linux-x86-64.so.2`/`ld-2.31.so`/etc, `*.py` matches the pwntools template. `pwninit` added to `blacklist.txt` at line 20894 between `pwned` and `pwpolicy` (sort verified position-by-position: at index 3 `pwned`'s 'e' (101) < `pwninit`'s 'i' (105), and at index 2 `pwninit`'s 'n' (110) < `pwpolicy`'s 'p' (112) so it remains at the end of the `pwn*` block before `pwp*` begins). LC_ALL=C sort verified.

Single-file completion `_kp` covers VMware Tanzu's kpack CLI — a K8s-native image builder driven by Cloud Native Buildpacks specs. 14 top-level subcommands via `_subcmds`: `build`, `builder`, `buildpack`, `clusterbuilder`, `clusterbuildpack`, `clusterlifecycle`, `clusterstack`, `clusterstore`, `completion`, `config`, `image`, `import`, `secret`, `version`, `help`. 6 shared persistent flags via `_global` re-applied per leaf: `-h/--help`, `--kubeconfig FILE`, `--context CONTEXT`, `-n/--namespace NS`, `--registry-ca-cert-path FILE`, `--registry-verify-certs`. **Shared 6-action CRD pattern** `_crd_actions` (create/delete/list/patch/save/status) reused across builder/buildpack/clusterbuilder/clusterbuildpack/clusterlifecycle/clusterstack/clusterstore — single shared array means a future kpack API addition (e.g. a new clusterlifecycle action) cascades to all CRD-style subtrees. **Per-subtree specialization**: `image` adds a 7th action `trigger` (force a new build), with `create`/`save` carrying 16 flags (source-trio mutex via `--git`/`--blob`/`--local-path` plus `--git-revision`, `--registry`, `--cluster-builder`/`--builder`, `--service-account`, `--sub-path`, repeatable `*--env key=value` + `*--delete-env`, repeatable `*--cache-size`, `--additional-tag`, `--wait`, `--dry-run`, `--output yaml|json`); `config` is a 2-key K/V tree (`default-repository` and `default-service-account`); `import` covers `-f/--filename FILE`, `--show-changes` (dry-run-style preview), `--force` (overwrite); `completion` takes bash/fish/powershell/zsh. **Live-resource helper `_kp_resources`** runs `kubectl get <CRD-fully-qualified-kind> -o name` per CRD family — `images.kpack.io`, `builders.kpack.io`, `clusterbuilders.kpack.io`, `clusterbuildpacks.kpack.io`, `clusterlifecycles.kpack.io`, `clusterstacks.kpack.io`, `clusterstores.kpack.io`, `buildpacks.kpack.io` — and strips the `<kind>/` prefix so resource-name positionals auto-complete from the live cluster. **Blacklist additions (2)**: `kp` and `kpack` inserted between `koyeb` and `kpackagetool5` (sort verified: at index 1 'o' < 'p', then shorter-string-wins gives `kp` (length 2) < `kpack` (length 5) < `kpackagetool5` (length 13)). - **ptw (pytest-watch — fs-watch-and-rerun harness for pytest)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh`) — flags transcribed directly from upstream [github.com/joeyespo/pytest-watch](https://github.com/joeyespo/pytest-watch) README options table. Single-file completion `_ptw` covers Joe Esposito's pytest-watch — watches the filesystem and re-runs pytest on change. 19 flags total; unknown extra args pass through to pytest. Meta `-h/--help`, `-V/--version`. Watcher filtering: repeatable `*--ignore DIR` (file-set walker excludes), `--ext exts` (comma-separated `.py`/`*.pyx`/etc that trigger re-runs — default `.py`, `*` allows any), `--config FILE` (override implicit config-file lookup). Trigger control: `-c/--clear` (clear screen before each run), `-n/--nobeep`, `-w/--wait` (let a run finish before re-triggering — opposed to default-interrupt-on-fs-event), `--spool ms` (re-run delay default 200ms — lets fs events queue up), `-p/--poll` (polling instead of inotify-style events — useful in VMs/Docker bind mounts). Hook commands (each completes via `_command_names -e`): `--beforerun` (pre-run), `--afterrun` (post-run; gets pytest exit code as `$1`), `--onpass`, `--onfail`, `--onexit`, `--runner` (override the default `pytest` command). Debugger: `--pdb` (start pdb on errors, also implies `--wait` to prevent pdb interruption). Verbosity mutex `-q/--quiet` ↔ `-v/--verbose` (with `--quiet` taking precedence per upstream — encoded as a single mutex group so zsh suppresses the dominated flag once the user has selected). Trailing `*:pytest path or pytest arg:_files` passes through to pytest's own argument parser. `ptw` added to `blacklist.txt` at line 20750 between `ptunnel` and `ptweens` (sort verified position-by-position: at index 2 `ptunnel`'s 'u' (117) < `ptw`'s 'w' (119), and at index 3 `ptw` ends while `ptweens`'s 'e' (101) is present — shorter-string-wins gives `ptw` < `ptweens`). LC_ALL=C sort verified.

- **tmuxinator + mux (Ruby YAML-driven tmux session manager, 2 binary stems)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh` — verified on this host that no shipped `_tmuxinator` is present, even though upstream documents installing one at `/usr/local/share/zsh/site-functions/_tmuxinator` from the gem) — subcommand inventory and config-file priority list extracted from the upstream [tmuxinator/tmuxinator README](https://github.com/tmuxinator/tmuxinator). Single-file completion `_tmuxinator` is multi-stem `#compdef tmuxinator mux` (the `mux` binary is upstream's short alias, same Thor app behind both names; `mux` was already at blacklist line 16805 with no file). 14 verbs covered with all aliases enumerated as separate `_describe` entries: `new`/`n`, `open`/`o`, `edit`/`e`, `start`/`s`, `copy`/`c`/`cp`, `list`/`l`/`ls`, `delete`/`rm`, `stop`, `stop-all`, `implode`/`i`, `doctor`, `debug`, `help`/`h`, `version` → 25 dispatch keys. Per-verb argument handling: `new`/`open` accept `-l/--local` (creates `.tmuxinator.yml` in cwd) plus project name; `edit` takes project name; `start`/`s` covers `-p/--project-config FILE` (explicit YAML via `_files -g "*.(yml|yaml)"`), `-n/--name` (session-name override), `--suppress-tmux-version-warning`, project positional, plus repeatable `*:override key:value` for Thor template substitution at launch; `copy`/`c`/`cp` takes 2 positionals (source project, new name); `delete`/`rm` accepts repeatable `*:project name`; `stop` takes one project; `debug` adds mutex `--cmd`/`--no-cmd` plus project + overrides; `doctor`/`implode`/`list`/`stop-all`/`version` take no positionals. Live-project helper `_tmuxinator_projects` walks all 4 documented config roots in upstream priority order — `$TMUXINATOR_CONFIG` (custom env), `$XDG_CONFIG_HOME/tmuxinator`, `$HOME/.config/tmuxinator`, `$HOME/.tmuxinator` — globs `*.yml`/`*.yaml` (zsh nullglob `(N)`), strips `:t:r` to bare project name, deduplicates with `${(u)…}`, and appends a synthetic `[local: ./.tmuxinator.yml]` marker entry when a local-project YAML is present. `tmuxinator` already at blacklist line 25890 and `mux` already at line 16805; no add needed.

- **resperf (DNS resolver perf testing tool — DNS-OARC dnsperf package)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh`) — flags transcribed directly from upstream [manpages.debian.org/bookworm/dnsperf/resperf.1](https://manpages.debian.org/bookworm/dnsperf/resperf.1.en.html). Single-file completion `_resperf` covers DNS-OARC's resolver-side load tester (sister to the authoritative-server-side `dnsperf` already in repo at `more_src/_dnsperf`). resperf ramps up query rate over a configurable ramp-up window, optionally sustains constant load after, and finds the throughput threshold under a target acceptable loss percentage. 27 flags covered: sources `-d FILE` (query input, `_files`; stdin if omitted), `-R` (reopen datafile if exhausted); target `-s HOST` (server, default 127.0.0.1, via `_hosts`), `-p PORT`, `-M MODE` (`udp`/`tcp`/`dot`/`doh`), `-f FAMILY` (`inet`/`inet6`/`any`); rate model `-m QPS` (target max, default 100000), `-r SECONDS` (ramp-up, default 60), `-c SECONDS` (constant-rate hold after ramp, default 0), `-L PERCENT` (max acceptable loss for throughput determination), `-q N` (max outstanding per client, default 64k), `-F N` (fall-behind limit, default 1000; 0=disable); client model `-C N` (clients with separate sockets), `-a ADDR` (local source addr via `_hosts`), `-x PORT` (local source port, default wildcard 0); EDNS/DNSSEC `-D` (DNSSEC OK bit, enables EDNS0), `-e` (EDNS0 OPT only); auth `-y [alg:]name:base64-secret` (TSIG); buffers `-b kB` (socket buffer); plotting `-i SECONDS` (data-point interval, default 0.5), `-P FILE` (output, default `resperf.gnuplot`); protocol-specific `*-O option=value` (repeatable, for DoT/DoH params); timeout `-t SECONDS` (default 45); output `-v` (verbose), `-W` (warnings to stdout); help `-h`. `resperf` added to `blacklist.txt` at line 22089 between `respberry` and `responder` (lexicographic-by-position-4: 'b' < 'e' < 'o'). LC_ALL=C sort verified.
- **powerstat (Canonical's power + thermal + CPU C-state monitor)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh`) — flags transcribed directly from upstream [manpages.ubuntu.com/manpages/jammy/man8/powerstat.8](https://manpages.ubuntu.com/manpages/jammy/man8/powerstat.8.html). Single-file completion `_powerstat` for Colin King's power-monitoring tool that reads either battery discharge rate or RAPL (Running Average Power Limit) domain counters. 19 flags covered: roll-up `-a` (= `-c -f -t -H`); sampling controls `-b` (redo if <98% CPU idle), `-d SECONDS` (start delay — defaults 180s on battery / 0s on RAPL), `-i PERCENT` (idle threshold for forced re-sample), `-p` (redo on any fork/exec/exit), `-r` (redo only if not-idle + fork/exec/exit), `-S` (standard averaging instead of rolling); data collection `-c` (per-CPU C-state activity), `-D` (all power-domain readings), `-f` (avg frequency across on-line cores), `-g` (Intel i915 GPU power), `-H` (histogram of power measurements), `-R` (switch from battery to RAPL source), `-t` (thermal-zone temperatures), `-z` (ignore zero readings); output `-n` (no column headings); log `-s` (dump fork/exec/exit log at end); `-h` (help). Positional args: `1: delay seconds`, `2: number of samples`. `powerstat` added to `blacklist.txt` at line 20239 between `powershell-empire` and `powertop` (lexicographic-by-position-6: 'h' < 's' < 't'). - **pacapt (universal pacman-style package-manager wrapper)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh`) — operation/flag inventory extracted directly from upstream [github.com/icy/pacapt](https://github.com/icy/pacapt) README. Single-file completion `_pacapt` for the pacman-API wrapper that translates `-S/-R/-Q/-U` operations into the host system's native package manager (apt/dnf/yum/zypper/brew/portage/pkg/etc). Top-level operation enumeration uses `_alternative` to multiplex two surfaces: **33-op pacman-style fused flag tree** via `_ops` describe (`-S` install, `-Sy` refresh DB, `-Su` upgrade, `-Suy`/`-Syu` refresh+upgrade, `-Ss` search, `-Si`/`-Sii` info/detailed-info, `-Sg` groups, `-Sl` list-repo, `-Sc`/`-Scc`/`-Sccc` cache cleanup graduations, `-Sw` download-only, `-R` remove, `-Rs` remove+deps, `-Rn` remove+configs, `-Rns` remove+deps+configs, `-Rdd` force-skip-dep-check, `-Q` query, `-Qs` query-by-pattern, `-Qi`/`-Qii` info, `-Ql` list-files, `-Qo` owner-of-file, `-Qm` foreign packages, `-Qu` upgradeable, `-Qd` dependencies, `-Qe` explicit-installs, `-Qc` changelog, `-Qk` integrity-verify, `-U` local-file install, `-P` list-supported-ops); **7-alias long-form tree** via `_aliases` describe (`install`/`remove`/`search`/`upgrade`/`update`/`autoremove`/`clean`). Shared `_global` array (6 modifier flags) re-applied per-op: `-h/--help`, `-V/--version`, `--noconfirm`, `-q/--quiet`, `-y` (auto-yes alias), `-w` (download-only alias). Per-op argument handling: install/upgrade/sw/info/list ops accept package args via `_pacapt_remote` helper (deferred — no remote lookup, pacapt already translates underneath); search/`-Ss`/`-Qs` accept free-form pattern; remove/`-Q*` query ops complete from live `pacapt -Qq` via `_pacapt_installed` helper; `-Qo` completes file paths via `_files`; `-U` completes local package files via `_files -g "*.(deb|rpm|pkg.tar.{zst,xz,gz}|apk|tgz)"` glob covering Debian/RPM/Arch-zst/Arch-xz/Arch-gz/Alpine/tarball; cache cleanup ops (`-Sc`/`-Scc`/`-Sccc`/`autoremove`/`clean`) and `update`/`-P` take no positional args. `pacapt` added to `blacklist.txt` at line 18571 between `pac` and `pacaptr` (Rust rewrite — distinct binary already covered). LC_ALL=C sort verified.

Image input completion uses `_files -g "*.(#i)(jpg|jpeg|png|gif|bmp|tif|tiff|webp|heic|heif|avif|svg|pdf|psd|tga|xpm|xbm|pnm|ppm|pgm|pbm|png|ico|jp2|jxr|jxl|dds|dpx|exr|hdr|miff|mng|sgi|yuv|xcf|wmf|mvg)"` for case-insensitive multi-format matching. `gm` already at blacklist line 9519 (between `glx-utils` and `gm2`); no add needed.

Live-resource completion helper `_tkn_k_resources` calls `kubectl get <kind> -o name` and strips the `<kind>/` prefix — used for all `describe`/`logs`/`delete`/`cancel`/`start` resource-name positionals across all 9 CRD families (`pipelines.tekton.dev`, `pipelineruns.tekton.dev`, `tasks.tekton.dev`, `taskruns.tekton.dev`, `eventlisteners.triggers.tekton.dev`, `clustertriggerbindings.triggers.tekton.dev`, `triggerbindings.triggers.tekton.dev`, `triggertemplates.triggers.tekton.dev`, `customruns.tekton.dev`). `tkn` already at blacklist line 25849 (between previously-installed `tknewsbiff` neighborhood); no add needed.
- **limactl (Lima — Linux VMs on Mac CLI)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh`) — flags derived directly from upstream `cmd/limactl/*.go` cobra command definitions in [lima-vm/lima](https://github.com/lima-vm/lima) plus [lima-vm.io/docs/reference/limactl/](https://lima-vm.io/docs/reference/limactl/). Single-file completion `_limactl` covers the full subcommand tree from `newApp()` (32 subcommands enumerated): `create`, `start`, `stop`, `restart`, `shell`, `copy` (alias `cp`), `list` (alias `ls`), `delete` (alias `rm`), `validate`, `prune`, `hostagent`, `guest-install`, `info`, `show-ssh`, `debug`, `edit`, `factory-reset`, `disk` (sub-sub: create/delete/list/resize/unlock), `usernet`, `gen-doc`, `gen-schema`, `snapshot` (sub-sub: create/delete/apply/list), `protect`/`unprotect`, `tunnel`, `template` (sub-sub: copy/ls/validate), `sudoers`, `start-at-login`, `network` (list/start/stop/reload/sudoers), `clone`, `rename`, `watch`, `yq-restrictions-help`. Plugin commands dynamically discovered via `addPluginCommands()` are not enumerated. Global persistent flags via shared `_global` array (5 flags): `--log-level` (trace/debug/info/warn/error), `--log-format` (text/json), `--debug`, `--tty` (auto-detected from stdout), `-y/--yes` (alias of `--tty=false`). Per-subcommand flag coverage: `start`/`create` (`--name`, `--list-templates`, `--list-drivers`, repeatable `*--set yq-expr`, `--foreground`, `--timeout`, `--progress`), `shell` (`--shell` via `_command_names -e`, `--workdir`, `--reconnect`, `--preserve-env`, `--start`, `--sync host-path`), `list` (`-f/--format` json/yaml/table/go-template, `--json` legacy alias, `--list-fields`, `--all-fields`, `-q/--quiet` table-only, repeatable `*--yq`, repeatable `*-l/--filter` AND-combined), `copy`/`cp` (`-r/--recursive`), `stop` (`-f/--force`), `delete` (`-f/--force`), `show-ssh` (`-f/--format` cmd/args/options/config), `validate` (`--fill`), `prune` (`--keep-referred`), `snapshot` (state machine: create/delete/apply/list with `--tag`), `template` (state machine: copy/ls/validate), `disk` (state machine with `--size`, `--format` qcow2/raw), `network`, `sudoers --check`, `start-at-login --enabled`, `gen-doc --type man/markdown/rest/yaml + --output`, `gen-schema --output`, `tunnel --ssh-flag`. Helper `_limactl_instances` runs `limactl list --quiet` for live instance-name completion across `shell`/`stop`/`delete`/`restart`/`copy`/`edit`/`show-ssh`/`protect`/`unprotect`/`clone`/`rename`/`tunnel`/`factory-reset`/`start-at-login`. `limactl` was already in `blacklist.txt` line 13768 (between `lima` and `limit`) but no completion file existed; this round fills the gap. The `_lima` wrapper completion already exists in more_src.
- **git-revise (pure-Python git history rewriter)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh`) — flags derived from upstream `gitrevise/tui.py` argparse plus [git-revise.readthedocs.io/en/latest/man.html](https://git-revise.readthedocs.io/en/latest/man.html). Single-file completion `_git-revise` for Michael Sullivan's efficient non-interactive history editor (update/split/rearrange commits without rebase mechanics). Three mutually exclusive groups encoded in `_arguments`: **autosquash** (`--autosquash` / `--no-autosquash`, controls `revise.autoSquash` config), **index** (`-a/--all` stage tracked / `-p/--patch` interactive hunks / `--no-index` ignore staged), **mode** (`-i/--interactive` edit commit stack / `-c/--cut` split commit / `-m/--message` reword non-interactively). Standalone flags: `-e/--edit` open editor for message, `--reauthor` reset author to current user, `--ref REF` target branch (defaults `HEAD`, completes with `__git_references`). `-m/--message` uses `append` action so it is repeatable for multi-line messages. Positional arg is target commit completed via `__git_revisions`. `--version` shows version and exits. `git-revise` was already reserved in `blacklist.txt` (line 9362, between `git-review` and `git-router`) by an earlier harvest run but the completion file was missing — this round fills the gap.

Dispatches on `$service` for direct sub-binaries vs the `rtla` umbrella. 3 tools (`osnoise`/`timerlat`/`hwnoise`) × 2 display modes (`top` real-time stream / `hist` histogram). 22 shared flags from `_shared` array: `-a/--auto`, `-p/--period US`, `-r/--runtime US`, `-s/--stop US` and `-S/--stop-total US` stopping thresholds, `-T/--threshold US` (default 5us), `-t/--trace FILE` save stopped trace, `-c/--cpus`/`-H/--house-keeping` CPU placement, `-d/--duration` time-unit suffixes, `-D/--debug`, repeatable `*-e/--event sys:event` + `*--filter` + `*--trigger`, `-P/--priority o:prio|r:prio|f:prio|d:runtime:period`, `-C/--cgroup`, `--warm-up SEC`, `--trace-buffer-size kB`, `--on-threshold`/`--on-end` action hooks, `-q/--quiet`, `-h/--help`. timerlat-specific `_timerlat_only` array (12 flags): `-i/--irq US`, `--thread US`, `--stack US`, 3-way thread mutex `-k/--kernel-threads` / `-u/--user-threads` (default) / `-U/--user-load`, `--dma-latency`, `--deepest-idle-state N`, `--bpf-action BPF-PROG`, `--stack-format truncate|skip|full`, `--no-aa`, `--aa-only US`. hist-only `_hist_only` array (6 flags): `-b/--bucket-size` (1), `-E/--entries` (256), `--no-header`/`--no-summary`/`--no-index`, `--with-zeros`. The `case $service in` dispatches to direct-binary mode (1 positional for top/hist) or umbrella `rtla` mode (2 positionals: tool then mode). 4 binaries added to blacklist.

- **skarnet s6-rc + s6-networking + s6-dns continuation (5 NEW files, 6 binaries)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh`) — all from skarnet.org software docs. `s6-rc-compile` (compile s6-rc service definitions into binary DB; 5 flags `-q` qualify domain per /etc/resolv.conf suffixes (env `$DNSQUALIFY`), mutex `-h`/`-H` /etc/hosts use (default `-H`), `-r` random-permute results, `-t MS` timeout (exit 99 if exceeded); repeatable positional domain), `s6-dnsname` (reverse DNS — IP → name; auto-detects IPv4/v6 from input; 6 flags: mutex `-4`/`-6` force version, mutex `-h`/`-H` /etc/hosts (default `-H`), `-r` random-permute, `-t MS` timeout). NOTE: existing previous-round `_s6-applyuidgid`/`_s6-envuidgid`/`_s6-setuidgid`/`_s6-softlimit`/`_s6-tai64n`/`_s6-tcpserver4` still active. `s6-applyuidgid` (drop privileges then exec; 5 flags `-u UID`, `-g GID`, `-G CSV-gidlist`, `-U` read UID/GID/GIDLIST env vars (cmdline overrides), `-z` unexport env vars), `s6-envuidgid` (set UID/GID/GIDLIST env vars from an account name then exec; 6 flags 3-way mutex `-u`/`-g`/`-B` user/group/user:group interpretation, `-n` numeric fallback, `-i` insist (exit 1 if unknown), `-D uid:gid:gidlist` default values), `s6-setuidgid` (switch to account's UID/GID/GIDLIST then exec — NO FLAGS upstream; takes only account positional + program args), `s6-softlimit` (apply setrlimit() limits then exec; 14 flags — modifier mutex `-H` set hard+soft / `-h` hard only; resource limits `-a` total memory, `-c` core file size, `-d` heap, `-f` file size, `-l` locked memory, `-m` all memory, `-o` open FDs, `-P` RT priority, `-p` procs per user, `-r` physical memory, `-s` stack, `-t` CPU seconds; each numeric option accepts `=` to mean "set to hard limit"), `s6-tai64n` + `s6-tai64nlocal` (multi-stem `#compdef s6-tai64n s6-tai64nlocal` — filters that prepend TAI64N timestamps to stdin lines; NO FLAGS upstream; `s6-tai64nlocal` converts TAI64N → local time), `s6-tcpserver4` + `s6-tcpserver6` (multi-stem TCP server runners IPv4/IPv6, exec per-connection program; 9 flags: `-1` print bound port to stdout for readiness, `-v 0/1/2` verbosity, `-c` max concurrent connections default 40 max 1000, `-C` per-IP cap default 40, `-b` backlog, `-G`/`-g`/`-u`/`-U` privilege dropping (root only)). Positional `<bind-IP> <port> <program> [args...]`.

- **Argus network-flow client family (ra/ratop/ralabel/rasort/racount/rasplit)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh`) — `_ra` multi-stem `#compdef ra ratop ralabel rasort racount rasplit` covers the QoSient argus-clients suite for network flow record analysis. Single file with shared `_ra_common` array containing the 28 base ra(1) options (`-A` agg-stats, `-b` dump-compiled-match-code, `-c CHAR` delim, `-D 1-8` debug level, `-d` daemon toggle, `-e REGEX` user-data match, `-E FILE` rejected-records output, `-F CONF` config source, `-h` help, `-H` abbreviate numerics, `-L N` header label frequency, `-n` number-to-name toggle, `-N N` first-N-records, `-p DIGITS` float precision, `-q` quiet, `*-r FILE` read argus data (repeatable, `*.argus`/`*.arg`), `-R DIR` recurse dir, `*-s FIELD` print-fields (repeatable: stime/saddr/daddr/sport/dport/proto/bytes/...), `-S URI` remote source `[user[:pass]@]host[:port]`, `-t TIMERANGE` time filter, `-T SECS` remote-read duration, `-u` Unix-time format, `-w FILE` append output (argus format), `-X` reset to defaults, `-z` TCP-state status field, `-Z s|d|b` actual TCP flag values). Then `case $service` dispatches tool-specific flags: `ratop` adds `-m` aggregation object (28 choices: srcid/smac/dmac/saddr/daddr/matrix/proto/sport/dport/...) + `-M correct|nocorrect|preserve|nopreserve|norep|rmon|nocurses` curses mode; `ralabel` adds `-f LABEL_SPEC_FILE` + `-M ADDR` simple-list mode + `-m saddr|daddr|saddr,daddr` IANA label target; `rasort` adds repeatable `*-m FIELD` sort key (35 choices: stime/ltime/dur/bytes/pkts/saddr/daddr/sport/dport/scc/dcc/sas/das/...) + `-M replace` in-place overwrite; `racount` adds `-M proto|addr` count breakdown (IPv4/IPv6 unicast/multicast addr type, IP/ether/ARP/RARP protos); `rasplit` adds `-M MODE` for partitioning. All variants accept BPF-style filter expression as `*` positional. Verified via argus-client(1) Debian manpages (ratop.1/ralabel.1/rasort.1/racount.1/ra.1). NOTE: existing `_argus` covers the argus(8) collector daemon itself separately.

REQUIRED `-ts` timestamp / `-proto tcp|udp|icmp` / `-src.ip` / `-dst.ip` + optional `-src.port` / `-dst.port` / `-duration 1ns` default), `slice` (-r/-w/-x index file/-from time/-to time/-p proto), `ts` (-r/-w timestamps). - **ply (lightweight Linux BPF tracer, dtrace/awk-style) + tcpsnitch (LD_PRELOAD sockets API tracer)** (dup-checked clean against `/usr/share/zsh` + `/opt/homebrew/share/zsh` + `/usr/local/share/zsh`) — `ply` (wkz/ply from src/ply/ply.c getopt_long — Tobias Waldekranz's lightweight dynamic Linux tracer. Compiles dtrace/awk-style scripts to BPF via kprobes/tracepoints; only libc required at runtime. Multi-arch (x86_64/aarch64/arm/loongarch/mips/riscv32/riscv64/powerpc). 9 flags: `-h/--help`, `-v/--version`, `-c/--command CMD` (run shell command + exit when done), `-d/--debug`, `-e/--dry-run` (compile-only — no BPF load), `-k/--keep-going` (tolerate trace-buffer overruns), `-S/--dump` (show generated BPF), `-T/--self-test`, `-u/--unbuffer` (force stdout/stderr unbuffered); positional ply script e.g. `'kretprobe:vfs_read { @["size"] = quantize(retval); }'`), `tcpsnitch` (GregoryVds/tcpsnitch from bin/tcpsnitch bash getopts — LD_PRELOAD-based sockets API tracer that intercepts libc network calls. Records tcp_info socket option at user-defined intervals + .pcap per socket. Two modes: Linux (run app directly) or Android (API 23+ via `-a` launch + `-k` kill+pull). 14 flags: `-h` help, `--version`, `-a` Android launch, `-k PKG` Android kill+pull, `-b BYTES` tcp_info dump every N bytes (default 0=off), `-c` pcap capture (Linux only), `-d DIR` trace output dir (default random `/tmp` dir), `-f LEVEL` file log verbosity 0-5 (default 2), `-l LEVEL` stderr log verbosity 0-5 (default 2), `-n` no upload to tcpsnitch.org, `-p` pedantic confirmation mode, `-t MSEC` JSON dump interval (default 1000ms), `-u USEC` tcp_info dump every N µs (default 0=off), `-v` verbose; positional `<app> [<args>]` is the command/package to instrument). Disk-pressure note: `_tcpsnitch` was written via Bash heredoc as a workaround after the Write tool hit ENOSPC at 99.9% disk usage — the underlying volume had only 945Mi free of 926Gi.

high-level driver `squashfuse` supports `-o offset=N`/`-o subdir=PATH`/`-o notify_pipe=PATH` plus FUSE pass-through (`-o ro`/`-o allow_other`/`-o allow_root`/`-o default_permissions`/`-o direct_io`/`-o kernel_cache`/`-o auto_cache`/`-o uid=N`/`-o gid=N`/`-o umask=M`); low-level `squashfuse_ll` adds `-o timeout=N` idle-auto-unmount + `-o uid=N`/`-o gid=N` file-owner mapping; `squashfuse_ls` takes a single ARCHIVE positional with no flags; `squashfuse_extract` takes `ARCHIVE PATH_TO_EXTRACT` or `ARCHIVE -a` for whole-archive extraction).

(`-d/--dry-run`), select (`-e/--expression` selector + `--show-traits` + `--vars`)).

Directory layout:

```
src/              main completions
more_src/         additional completions
man_src/          completions parsed from man pages
override_src/     overrides (prepended to fpath)
architecture_src/ cross-architecture toolchains
```

---

## [0x01] // JACK IN

### Zinit `[RECOMMENDED]`

> `~/.zshrc`

```sh
source "$HOME/.zinit/bin/zinit.zsh"
zinit ice lucid nocompile wait'0e' nocompletions
zinit load MenkeTechnologies/zsh-more-completions
```

> **NOTE:** The `nocompletions` ice prevents zinit from symlinking all completions into `~/.zinit/completions`. Instead the plugin directly manipulates `fpath` — this lets `override_src` completions take priority over defaults while keeping system completions untouched.

### Oh My Zsh

```sh
cd "$HOME/.oh-my-zsh/custom/plugins" && git clone https://github.com/MenkeTechnologies/zsh-more-completions.git
```

Add `zsh-more-completions` to your plugins array in `~/.zshrc`.

OMZ only adds plugin root to fpath, so completions in subdirectories won't load without intervention. You need to wire the nested source dirs into fpath **before** OMZ runs `compinit`:

```sh
# OMZ does not add nested comp dirs to fpath so do it here, assume *src has completions
for plug in ${plugins[@]}; do
    if [[ -d "$ZSH/custom/plugins/$plug" ]]; then
        # null glob - no error
        for dir in "$ZSH/custom/plugins/$plug/"*src(N); do
            if [[ -d "$dir" ]]; then
                if [[ -z ${fpath[(r)$dir]} ]];then
                    if [[ $dir = *override* ]]; then
                        fpath=($dir $fpath)
                    else
                        fpath=($fpath $dir)
                    fi
                fi
            fi
        done
    fi
done
```

### Manual Install

```sh
git clone https://github.com/MenkeTechnologies/zsh-more-completions.git
```

Copy all `_*` files from the source directories to somewhere on your `fpath`.

---

## [0x02] // BOOT SEQUENCE

After install, initialize the completion system:

```sh
autoload -Uz compinit && compinit
```

For faster shell startup, cache the `~/.zcompdump`:

```sh
compinit -C
```

This skips the security check and loads the cached dump directly — **dramatically** faster boot times.

---

## [0x03] // STATS

Counts change constantly; **do not** edit totals by hand. From the repo root:

```sh
zsh scripts/print-repo-stats.zsh
```

This prints `_`-prefixed completion file counts per directory, `total_completions`, and `zunit_tests` (number of `@test` entries under `tests/`).

| Metric | How it is obtained |
|---|---|
| Completion files per dir | `scripts/print-repo-stats.zsh` (uses `find … -name '_*'`) |
| ZUnit tests | `grep '^@test' tests/*.zsh \| wc -l` (same as script output) |
| Generation method | Python scripts parsing `--help` + man pages |
| License | See `license.md` |

---

## [0x04] // TESTING

From the repository root, with [ZUnit](https://github.com/MenkeTechnologies/zunit) on your `PATH`:

```sh
zunit tests/*.zsh
```

GitHub Actions runs the same command on Ubuntu. On macOS, a wrong-case path can still `stat` the file; entries in `tests/t-more-src-existence.zsh` must use the exact basename as on disk (e.g. `_linguist`, not `_Linguist`) so Linux CI passes. `tests/t-repo-invariants.zsh` locks down repo metadata: `blacklist.txt` integrity, `.github/workflows/ci.yml` contract, `license.md`, and absence of tracked `.zwc` files.
